            interstitial: googletag.sizeMapping()
                .addSize([0, 0], [640, 480])
                .build()

        gptPage = window.digitalData && digitalData.page && digitalData.page.page ? digitalData.page.page : "blank";
        gptSubPage = window.digitalData && digitalData.page && digitalData.page.subPage ? digitalData.page.subPage : "blank";

        function gptClean(gptText) {
            if (typeof (gptText) == "string") {
                gptText = gptText.replace(/\&/g, '%26');
                return gptText.replace(/\^|\*|#|\$|\"|\'|\=|\,|\!|\+|\~|\;|\(|\)|\<|\>|\[|\]|\?|\%|\:|\@|\;|\&|\||\{|\}|\\|/g, '');
            }
            return "blank";
        }

        googletag.pubads()
            .setTargeting('property', 'value-of-property')    // Change and duplicate this line for as many additional keywords to send
            .setTargeting('doi', gptClean('10.1002/smll.202407829')) // Publication DOI
            .setTargeting('pbPage', gptClean(gptPage))
            .setTargeting('pbSubPage', gptClean(gptSubPage))
            .setTargeting('urlpath', gptClean(document.location.pathname));

        googletag.defineSlot($GooglePublisherCategory, 'fluid', 'advert-leaderboard')
            .defineSizeMapping(sizes.leaderboard)

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/templates/jsp/pb2/js/plugin/thiss-ds.js" nonce="746967a7fbbd451f8ebd9fe62cb79231"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="746967a7fbbd451f8ebd9fe62cb79231">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: '47b97eda-2233-4fd8-9510-912512117717'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

        (function() {
            function riskifiedBeaconLoad() {
                var store_domain = 'https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com';
                var session_id = '77A1775CFE172CEF5C01A431D5B45BA6';
                var url = ('https:' == document.location.protocol ? 'https://' : 'http://')
                    + "beacon.riskified.com?shop=" + store_domain + "&sid=" + session_id;

                s.type = 'text/javascript';
                s.async = true;
                s.src = url;
                var x = document.getElementsByTagName('script')[0];
                x.parentNode.insertBefore(s, x);
            }
            if (window.attachEvent)
                window.attachEvent('onload', riskifiedBeaconLoad)
            else
                window.addEventListener('load', riskifiedBeaconLoad, false);
        })();

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d27232241" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>With a high theoretical capacity, the MnS anode, however, exhibits a rather complex sodium diffusion kinetics and poor mechanical stability that hinder its application in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs). In this work, a simple, economical, and scalable strategy is developed to inherently coat nanoporous MnS with a 3D N, S co-doped thin carbon layer by using commercially available MnCO<sub>3</sub> as precursors. Specifically, the strategy involves a two-step annealing process, which converts the MnCO<sub>3</sub> microparticles into nanoporous Mn<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> and MnS step by step. The 3D N, S codoped carbon layer is in situ formed during the second annealing process by first coating the nanoporous Mn<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> with a polyaniline layer. Due to the inherent 3D carbon protection and the strong electronic interaction between N, S dopants and MnS, the N, S codoped carbon protected MnS obtained at 900 °C (NS-C@MnS-900) anode displays a high specific capacity of 845&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, which is higher than all reported MnS-based SIB anodes. It also shows an outstanding cyclability and rate performance, maintaining a stable capacity of ≈493&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 1300 cycles at 10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, which is also the best according to knowledge. These exceptional electrochemical performances and the scalable/simple/low-cost synthesis make the NS-C@MnS-900 attractive for industry application.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202407829-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202407829-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>For a sustainable society, developing advanced energy production and storage technologies is of great significance and also facing great challenges.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0001_R_d27232233e370" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Nat. Energy.">1</a>-<a href="#smll202407829-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0005_R_d27232233e370" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">5</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> For decades, lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) have been widely used in new energy electric vehicles with their high energy density, large output power, and long cycle life. However, the lithium resources in the earth's crust are limited, which leads to the sustainability issue.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0006_R_d27232233e375" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Nanoscale">6</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Thus, sodium-ion battery (SIBs) are attracting much attention due to the abundant natural reserve of Na, lower cost, and similar operating mechanism to LIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0007_R_d27232233e380" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Nat. Energy.">7</a>, <a href="#smll202407829-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0008_R_d27232233e380" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Carbon Energy">8</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>To enhance SIB performance, such as capacity, cycling stability, and operation voltage, researchers have been devoted to developing various kinds of anode materials, including non-graphitic carbons, alloys, transition metal compounds, etc. Among them, transition metal sulfides (TMS) are attracting extensive attention because of their high theoretical capacity, abundant resources, structural flexibility, and good electrochemical properties.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0009_R_d27232233e388" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">9</a>-<a href="#smll202407829-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0013_R_d27232233e388" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Chem. Sci.">13</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> For example, eggshell structured N-doped FeS synthesized by Jiang et&nbsp;al.,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0014_R_d27232233e393" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - J. Colloid. Interf. Sci.">14</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> has a specific capacity of 520.1&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. A composite of layered nano-MoS<sub>2</sub> and micro-MXene prepared by Wen et&nbsp;al.,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0015_R_d27232233e405" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - J. Mater. Chem. A">15</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> exhibits a specific capacity of 612&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 600 cycles at 0.5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Among these metal sulfides, MnS is considered to be an ideal anode material for SIBs due to its high theoretical capacity (616&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0016_R_d27232233e417" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Nanoscale">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> low cost, good reversibility, and environmental friendliness.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0017_R_d27232233e422" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Int. J. Energy Res.">17</a>-<a href="#smll202407829-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0019_R_d27232233e422" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - J. Power Sources.">19</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> For example, MnS nanocubes encapsulated in sulfur-doped carbon matrix show a high reversible capacity of 600&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and a capacity of 357&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 1000 cycles at a large current density of 10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0020_R_d27232233e436" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Small">20</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Hollow spheres of γ-MnS/α-MnS heterojunction exhibit a capacity of 362.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 1000 cycle at 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0021_R_d27232233e446" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Chem. Eng. J.">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, similar to other metal sulfides, MnS-based anode usually has poor electronic conductivity and large volume change during the charge/discharge process, resulting in poor rate performance and limited cycle life.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0022_R_d27232233e451" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Nano-Micro. Lett.">22</a>-<a href="#smll202407829-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0025_R_d27232233e451" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> These issues may be solved by combining nanoscale MnS with carbon materials, especially with inherently coated 3D interconnected chemically doped carbon thin layer.</p>
         
         <p>For a long time, the research on MnS has been focused on the synthesis of nanoparticles with unique shape (such as spherical,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0026_R_d27232233e459" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - J. Energy Chem.">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> square,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0020_R_d27232233e464" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Small">20</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> bar,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0027_R_d27232233e469" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> flower structure,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0028_R_d27232233e475" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">28</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> etc.), however, these synthesis methods are usually too complex, involve the excess use of surfactants, or not suitable for large scale production. In order to forward the laboratory research into practical application, a facile and scalable fabrication strategy with low cost is urgently needed. In this work, from the perspective of industrialization, we developed a highly scalable strategy to prepare nanoporous MnS microparticles with inherently coated N, S codoped 3D interconnected carbon layer by using commercially available MnCO<sub>3</sub> microparticles as raw materials. Specifically, the purchased MnCO<sub>3</sub> without any pretreatment is annealed to form nanoporous Mn<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, which is then soaked in aniline to form a 3D polyaniline protection layer on the porous Mn<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>. Without any drying or rinsing, the samples are then annealed in the atmosphere of 2-aminothiophenol and argon at 900&nbsp;°C to realize the transformation of 3D polyaniline into 3D N, S-codoped carbon and Mn<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> into MnS, simultaneously (NS-C@MnS). The whole process is shown in <b>Scheme</b> <a href="#smll202407829-fig-0008">1</a>. Thanks to the 3D conductive porous carbon layer, the inherent coating, and the strong Mn-S and Mn-N bonds with the N, S-codoped carbon layer, the sodium storage performance of the NS-C@MnS is greatly enhanced, delivering a record-high capacity of 845&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. This value is the highest ever reported for MnS-based anodes. Moreover, it also manifests the best cycling and rate performances in comparison to reported results. A stable capacity of 492.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> can be maintained after even 1300 cycles.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smll202407829-fig-0008"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/1e6923d6-068c-4575-9635-1c46e753017e/smll202407829-fig-0008-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/1e6923d6-068c-4575-9635-1c46e753017e/smll202407829-fig-0008-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/0af270e7-a451-4099-8ed3-b8ca8945b3f0/smll202407829-fig-0008-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/1e6923d6-068c-4575-9635-1c46e753017e/smll202407829-fig-0008-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Scheme 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202407829-fig-0008&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202407829" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Schematic diagram showing the synthesis process of NS-C@MnS.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202407829-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202407829-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <p>To determine the phase structures at each step, X-ray powder diffraction (XRD) measurements were performed (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202407829-fig-0001">1a</a>). The XRD pattern showed that pure Mn<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> crystals were formed after annealing MnCO<sub>3</sub>. After the pyrolyzation treatment at 900 °C in the presence of 2-aminothiophenol, pure MnS phase was formed. Selected area electron diffraction (SAED) patterns further demonstrate the fabrication of well-crystallized MnS (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0001">1b</a>).</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smll202407829-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/0d44819d-33ec-4291-a38a-a98ec0b60654/smll202407829-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/0d44819d-33ec-4291-a38a-a98ec0b60654/smll202407829-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/833a52d3-76f4-4c7c-b7e7-b4770418c218/smll202407829-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/0d44819d-33ec-4291-a38a-a98ec0b60654/smll202407829-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202407829-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202407829" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) XRD patterns of MnCO<sub>3</sub>, Mn<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, and NS-C@MnS. b) SAED pattern of NS-C@MnS, c) SEM image of NS-C@MnS, d) STEM-EDS images of NS-C@MnS. e) STEM and f) STEM-EDS image of etched NS-C@MnS.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Scanning electron microscopy (SEM) characterization shows that after the two-step annealing treatment, the obtained NS-C@MnS microparticles show no observable shape or size change compared with the original MnCO<sub>3</sub> particles with varying sizes of micrometer scale (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1a,c</a>, Supporting Information). Transmission electron microscopy (TEM) characterization reveals that 3D nanoporous structure is formed in the Mn<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> particles due to the decomposition reaction by releasing CO<sub>2</sub> (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1c</a>, Supporting Information). Scanning transmission electron microscopy (STEM) image shows that the nanoporous structure is retained after the formation of MnS from Mn<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0001">1d</a>). STEM-based energy dispersive spectroscopy (EDS) mapping further confirms that Mn, S, and C elements are uniformly distributed in the nanoporous NS-C@MnS (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0001">1d</a>). To demonstrate the inherent 3D protection by the conductive carbon layer, we used 2&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> HCl solution to remove MnS. STEM characterization demonstrates the interconnected nanoporous nanotubular-like 3D carbon skeleton was formed with a channel diameter of about 20–30&nbsp;nm (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0001">1e</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0029_R_d27232233e615" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - ACS Appl. Nano Mater.">29</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> STEM-EDS mapping demonstrates the homogeneous distributions of C, N, and S elements in 3D nanoporous tubular-like carbon (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0001">1f</a>). Some residual MnS nanoparticles can also be observed, which is hard to be completely remove probably due to the strong Mn–S and Mn–N interaction with the 3D carbon.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0030_R_d27232233e623" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - ACS Materials Lett">30</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>The chemical states of elements on the NS-C@MnS were studied by X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS). <b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202407829-fig-0002">2a</a> shows that the main elements in NS-C@MnS are Mn, S, N, and C. The high-resolution XPS spectrum of Mn 2p shows two representative peaks of Mn<sup>2+</sup> at 641.06 and 652.77&nbsp;eV. The peak located at 643.1&nbsp;eV is endorsed to the C─S─Mn bond,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0020_R_d27232233e638" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Small">20</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> which represents the bond between MnS and the 3D nanoporous carbon (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0002">2b</a>). The XPS spectrum of S 2p shows the binding energies at 160.72 and 161.95&nbsp;eV, corresponding to the S 2p<sup>3/2</sup> and S 2p<sup>1/2</sup> peaks of Mn─S bond, respectively. The peaks at 163.5 and 168.29&nbsp;eV can be assigned to C─S and C─SO<sub>n</sub> bonds, respectively, demonstrating the doping of S in the 3D porous carbon (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0002">2c</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0031_R_d27232233e657" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - Small">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> N 1s spectrum indicates the presence of pyridine N (397.98&nbsp;eV), pyrrole N (399.48&nbsp;eV), graphite N (400.98&nbsp;eV), and oxidized N (401.98&nbsp;eV) in the carbon matrix (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0002">2d</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0032_R_d27232233e665" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Sci. Total Environ.">32</a>-<a href="#smll202407829-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0035_R_d27232233e665" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - J. Energy Chem.">35</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The Mn-N at 399.2&nbsp;eV may also exist.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0036_R_d27232233e670" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - ACS Nano">36</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> These dopants/defects in the carbon network would provide a large number of active sites for sodium ions diffusion/storage. In the C1s spectrum, the C─C/C═C characteristic peak is at 284.8&nbsp;eV. Some other bonds such as C─N/C─S (≈285.9 eV), C─O and C═O bonds can also be observed (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0037_R_d27232233e679" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - Carbon Energy">37</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smll202407829-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/2c9e9bae-3db2-470b-b38b-2d22e09165f9/smll202407829-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/2c9e9bae-3db2-470b-b38b-2d22e09165f9/smll202407829-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/72d368ea-5899-4a49-be5b-b4b1a838774b/smll202407829-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/2c9e9bae-3db2-470b-b38b-2d22e09165f9/smll202407829-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202407829-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202407829" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) XPS survey spectra of NS-C@MnS. High-resolution b) Mn 2p region; c) S 2p region; and d) N 1s region.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>N<sub>2</sub> adsorption-desorption isothermal curve shows that the NS-C@MnS has a specific surface area of 7.7&nbsp;m<sup>2&nbsp;</sup>g<sup>−1</sup> (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202407829-fig-0003">3a</a>) and a wide range of pore size less than 100&nbsp;nm (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0003">3b</a>). Based on the STEM observation, the pore size of ≈50&nbsp;nm should be corresponding to the nanoporous MnS structure and the pore size of less than 5&nbsp;nm may be originated from the 3D carbon layer.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smll202407829-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/bca68e58-53a1-4d6d-a133-0b93eafcada3/smll202407829-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/bca68e58-53a1-4d6d-a133-0b93eafcada3/smll202407829-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/9f0876ec-c6eb-4325-b2e5-08e3168b17be/smll202407829-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/bca68e58-53a1-4d6d-a133-0b93eafcada3/smll202407829-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202407829-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202407829" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Nitrogen adsorption/desorption isotherms and b) pore size distribution of NS-C@MnS-900. c) XRD patterns and d) Raman spectra of NS-C@MnO, MnS-800, NS-C@MnS-900, and NS-C@MnS-1000.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Before the battery test, the effect of the second annealing temperature was explored. XRD patterns (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0003">3c</a>) show that carbon-coated MnO/MnS mixture (named as NS-C@MnO, MnS-800) is formed at 800&nbsp;°C. Carbon-coated pure MnS were obtained when annealed at 900 and 1000&nbsp;°C (NS-C@MnS-900, and NS-C@MnS-1000). Raman spectra (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0003">3d</a>) show that there is a strong peak located at 640&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup> for NS-C@MnO, MnS-800, which is attributed to the Mn–O vibration mode.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0038_R_d27232233e752" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - J. Mater. Chem. A">38</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the change of annealing temperature has no significant effect on the ratio of D/G peak, indicating that the coated 3D carbon structure on the surface of the synthesized MnS ligaments is relatively stable.</p>
         
         <p>When used as a potential SIB anode, the capacity of the three samples gradually increased with cycling as shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202407829-fig-0004">4a</a>. The initial low capacity is attributed to the fact that MnS nano-ligaments are tightly packed with carbon layers. Thus, a portion of MnS does not participate in the electrochemical reaction during the initial charge/discharge process.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0039_R_d27232233e766" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Nanoscale">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The gradual increase in the capacity with cycling should be caused by the cycling-induced activation, which is common in metal sulfide anode.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0040_R_d27232233e771" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> According to previous reports,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0039_R_d27232233e777" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Nanoscale">39</a>, <a href="#smll202407829-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0040_R_d27232233e777" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> the activation process is associated with gradually permeating electrolytes and the addition of new active surfaces or sites induced by particle comminution-reconstruction processes. In comparison, the sample prepared at 900&nbsp;°C (i.e., NS-C@MnS-900) exhibits a relatively higher capacity at both 0.1 and 2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. It can be seen that after 120 cycles at the current density of 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the capacity of NS-C@MnS-900 can reach 845&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, higher than that of NS-C@MnO, MnS-800 (646.4&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>), and NS-C@MnS-1000 (634&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>). Even at the initial cycling stage, when the current density is 0.1, 0.5, 1, 5, 10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, NS-C@MnS-900 exhibits a reversible capacity of 529.6, 420.1, 383, 270.5, 183.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, and when the current density is restored to 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the capacity can return to the original value (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0004">4c</a>). Moreover, the NS-C@MnS-900 can be stably cycled at a wide current density range from 0.1 to 100&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> with a high rate performance (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0004">4a–f</a>). We speculate that the greatly enhanced anode performance should be due to the strong C─S─Mn and C─N─Mn bond interaction which can greatly stabilize the nano-MnS besides the coating effect, accommodate the volume change, and inhibit the dissolution of polysulfide. As revealed in our previous work,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0036_R_d27232233e808" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - ACS Nano">36</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> it was determined through the analysis of the total density of states (TDOS) that the doping of N and S on the carbon layer can increase the density of states near the Fermi level of NS-C@MnS, contributing to faster electron transfer and enhanced electrochemical activity. More encouragingly, we find that the performance (both the capacity and cycling durability) of NS-C@MnS-900 exceeds those of all the reported MnS-based anodes (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0004">4g,h</a>; Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information)<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0016_R_d27232233e820" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Nanoscale">16</a>, <a href="#smll202407829-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0020_R_d27232233e820" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Small">20</a>-<a href="#smll202407829-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0022_R_d27232233e820" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Nano-Micro. Lett.">22</a>, <a href="#smll202407829-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0041_R_d27232233e820" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - J. Energy Storage.">41</a>, <a href="#smll202407829-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0042_R_d27232233e820" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Dalton Trans.">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> in SIBs and is also outstanding when compared with recently reported other metal sulfide-based anodes (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0004">4i</a>; Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0025_R_d27232233e831" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">25</a>, <a href="#smll202407829-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0043_R_d27232233e831" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - J. Mater. Chem. A">43</a>-<a href="#smll202407829-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0047_R_d27232233e831" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - Adv. Energy Mater.">47</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smll202407829-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/7abbc2a0-55a7-47a9-95dc-73c0c57a32dc/smll202407829-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/7abbc2a0-55a7-47a9-95dc-73c0c57a32dc/smll202407829-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/eba42f80-bf8f-413f-b0ac-71b06dc87c54/smll202407829-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/7abbc2a0-55a7-47a9-95dc-73c0c57a32dc/smll202407829-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202407829-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202407829" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Cycling performance of NS-C@MnO, MnS-800, NS-C@MnS-900, NS-C@MnS-1000 at current densities of a) 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, b) 2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. c) Rate capability of NS-C@MnO, MnS-800, NS-C@MnS-900, NS-C@MnS-1000 during the initial cycling stage and NS-C@MnS-900 during stable cycling stage. Cycling performance of NS-C@MnS-900 at current densities of d) 1, e) 10, and f) 100&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Comparing the performance of NS-C@MnS-900 (stable stage) with other g,h) MnS-based anodes, and i) TMSs anodes.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>To investigate the reaction mechanism, we first compared the initial 3 cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves of NS-C@MnS-900 (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202407829-fig-0005">5a</a>). In the discharge process, a reduction peak (a) appears at 1.96&nbsp;V during the first cycle, assigning to the reaction of the doped S in carbon with sodium ions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0048_R_d27232233e870" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Chem. Eng. J.">48</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The reduction peak (b) should be corresponded to the reversible reaction of Na<sup>+</sup> with the rich surface functional groups.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0049_R_d27232233e878" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - ACS Sustainable Chem. Eng.">49</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Another reduction peak (c) observed at 0.4&nbsp;V during the subsequent discharge is due to the formation of a solid electrolyte interface (SEI) layer along with the insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> into the MnS lattice, leading to a conversion reaction (MnS+2Na<sup>+</sup>+2e<sup>−</sup>→Na<sub>2</sub>S+Mn).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0020_R_d27232233e892" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Small">20</a>, <a href="#smll202407829-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0050_R_d27232233e892" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">50</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> A pair of sharp redox peaks (d/e) should be due to the insertion/extraction of Na<sup>+</sup> in the nanospace between the carbon layer and MnS.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0051_R_d27232233e899" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - Sustain. Energ. Fuels">51</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The sharp reduction peaks indicate that the synthesized carbon layer has a large interlayer spacing, which can accommodate a large amount of Na<sup>+</sup>. During charge, a wide oxidation peak (f) appears at 0.8&nbsp;V assigning to the desodiation of the surface functional groups.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0049_R_d27232233e907" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - ACS Sustainable Chem. Eng.">49</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The oxidation peak (g) at 1.67&nbsp;V should be corresponded to the reverse reaction of the doped S in carbon with sodium.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0048_R_d27232233e912" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Chem. Eng. J.">48</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The oxidation peak (h) at 2.1&nbsp;V may correspond to the reverse reaction of Mn to produce MnS (Mn+Na<sub>2</sub>S-2e<sup>−</sup>→MnS+2Na<sup>+</sup>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0050_R_d27232233e924" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">50</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the subsequent cycle, the reduction peak at 1.96&nbsp;V disappears and transforms into the peak at 1.56&nbsp;V, which might be due to the multi-step sulfidation process. The oxidation peak at 0.8&nbsp;V gradually becomes stronger, which could be attributed to the gradually increased reaction surface area with cycling. This also explains the gradually increased specific capacity with cycling. The oxidation peak at ≈1.66 V and 2.1&nbsp;V shift toward lower potentials, this could be attributed to the changes in the lattice structure caused by the insertion and extraction of Na<sup>+</sup>. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0005">5b</a> shows the first three charge/discharge curves of NS-C@MnS-900 at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. The first discharge capacity is 636&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, and the first charge capacity is 499&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, resulting in the Coulombic efficiency of 78.5% in the first circle. There is capacity decay after the initial cycle, which is mainly due to the SEI formation, and some irreversible reactions. During subsequent cycles, there is a continuous increase in capacity, accompanied by a gradual rightward shift in the charge–discharge curves (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>, Supporting Information). At different current densities (0.1–10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>), the charge/discharge curves of the NS-C@MnS-900 show similar shape (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0005">5c</a>), indicating that the storage behavior of sodium ions does not change much over a wide range of operating currents. The enhanced rate performance should be due to the highly conductive 3D continuous porous carbon coating. Moreover, the rich N and S sites in the 3D carbon are also beneficial to the Na<sup>+</sup> reaction kinetics.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smll202407829-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/0e6e71cf-d7d4-4d43-90e3-eb28f5f80afe/smll202407829-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/0e6e71cf-d7d4-4d43-90e3-eb28f5f80afe/smll202407829-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/d1c3046d-2f53-424b-8603-ec86fde371c7/smll202407829-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/0e6e71cf-d7d4-4d43-90e3-eb28f5f80afe/smll202407829-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202407829-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202407829" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) CV curves of NS-C@MnS-900 at 0.1&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> in the initial three cycles. b) Charge–discharge profiles of NS-C@MnS-900 at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. c) GCD curves of NS-C@MnS-900 at different current densities. d) Ex situ XRD patterns of NS-C@MnS-900 acquired during discharging and charging against Na metal at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. The corresponding voltage profile is shown on the left side of (d).</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <div class="paragraph-element">Ex situ XRD study shows that as the discharge went on, the diffraction peak of the (220) crystal plane of Na<sub>2</sub>S emerged (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0005">5d</a>), and the diffraction peaks from MnS weakened significantly when discharged to 0.01&nbsp;V, demonstrating the transformation process of MnS during discharge. During the subsequent charging, the weakened peaks from MnS become sharp again. At the same time, the diffraction peak from Na<sub>2</sub>S disappears, indicating the good reversibility of the battery reaction. Ex situ Raman spectra (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4a,b</a>, Supporting Information) show that the intensity of the G-band tends to decrease during the discharge process, reflecting the adsorption of Na at the carbon surface's pores, defects, and edges. The storage of Na<sup>+</sup> in the carbon layer suppresses the E<sub>2g</sub> in-plane bond-stretching motion of pairs of C sp<sup>2</sup> atoms, resulting in the decrease of G-band peak.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0052_R_d27232233e998" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - ChemSusChem">52</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the subsequent charge process, the intensity of the G-band recovers to its initial state, corresponding to the desodiation and the disappearance of Na<sup>+</sup> influence on the G-band. Based on the above discussion, the storage mechanism of sodium ions is described as follows:

         </div>
         
         <p>In order to reveal the kinetics origin and mechanism of the NS-C@MnS-900 electrode, CV curves at different scan rates are recorded. As shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202407829-fig-0006">6a</a>, the redox peaks only slightly shift and widen with the increase of the scanning rate, indicating that the electrode had a low polarization. The pseudocapacitive behavior is evaluated by using the Randles–Sevcik (R-S) equation, <i>i</i> = a<i>v</i><sup>b</sup>, in which <i>v</i> is the scan rate and <i>i</i> is the peak current. A b-value close to 0.5 represents a diffusion-controlled process; while, a capacitance-contributed process occurs when the b-value is close to 1. The b-values of the labeled peak I to peak IV are calculated to be 0.92, 0.86, 0.98, and 0.96, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0006">6b</a>), suggesting a predominant capacitive characteristic of the NS-C@MnS-900. can be distinguished using the equation <i>v</i> = k<sub>1</sub><i>v</i>+k<sub>2</sub><i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup>. The capacitance-controlled contribution is 73.9%, 79.2%, 82.2%, 83.5%, and 87.2% at the scan rates of 0.2, 0.4, 0.6, 0.8, and 1.0&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0006">6c,d</a>). The ratio of pseudocapacitance contribution gradually enhanced from 73.9% to 87.2% with the increase of scanning rate. Compared with other materials, it is evident that the process occurring on the NS-C@MnS-900 electrode is controlled by capacitance (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>, Supporting Information). One of the reasons is that the nanoscale MnS ligaments can improve the charge/discharge rates of Na<sup>+</sup>, resulting in enhanced kinetics of interfacial Na<sup>+</sup> storage. On the other hand, the nanoporous structure can facilitate mass transfer and the 3D carbon layer can improve the electronic conductivity.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smll202407829-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/4f27f97d-3190-4cef-942a-254ae4f53664/smll202407829-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>

         <div class="paragraph-element">We then used the galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) to characterize ion migration (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202407829-fig-0007">7a</a>) and get the diffusion coefficient of Na<sup>+</sup> (D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup>) in the NS-C@MnS-900 electrode (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0007">7c</a>). The D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> values can be evaluated by the formula:

         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smll202407829-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/77494321-1ab1-4969-a8ac-e63dcf836a1c/smll202407829-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/77494321-1ab1-4969-a8ac-e63dcf836a1c/smll202407829-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/f5ca704a-5a8c-41fc-bab7-eba4e633ca57/smll202407829-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/77494321-1ab1-4969-a8ac-e63dcf836a1c/smll202407829-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202407829-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202407829" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) GITT curves of NS-C@MnS-900, b) voltage response over time during a single current pulse, c) sodium ion diffusion coefficients of NS-C@MnS-900, d) Ex situ Nyquist plots of NS-C@MnS-900 acquired during discharging and charging against Na metal at a rate of 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and e)&nbsp;corresponding <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>, <i>R</i><sub>s</sub> values. f) Nyquist plots of NS-C@MnS-900 electrode before and after 500 cycles at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> from 0.01 to 10<sup>7</sup>&nbsp;Hz.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>During the sodiation/desodiation process, the lowest value of D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> is achieved in the charge/discharge voltage platforms, revealing the occurrence of phase transformation. The D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> during the discharge and charge process is calculated to be about 10<sup>−8</sup>–10<sup>−6</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0007">7c</a>). These values are several orders of magnitude larger than that of other MnS-based electrodes,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202407829-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202407829-bib-0020_R_d27232233e1296" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Small">20</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> suggesting that the doped 3D carbon skeleton can greatly facilitate Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics. Besides, the D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> of NS-C@MnS-900 (1.74&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−7</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>) is also higher than NS-C@MnO,MnS-800 (2.36&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−11</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>) and NS-C@MnS-1000 (3.78&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−11</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>) (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a>, Supporting Information). From the EIS test (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0007">7d</a>), the corresponding solid-state diffusion resistance (<i>R</i><sub>S</sub>) does not change much, indicating that the structure of the battery is stable (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0007">7e</a>). The charge transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>CT</sub>) first decreased with the discharge and then remained stable during charge (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0007">7e</a>). It is suggested that an effective electrochemical activation process occurred during the discharge. After 500 cycles at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the shape of the EIS curve does not change, however, the <i>R</i><sub>CT</sub> value decreases obviously from 10.96 to 2.20&nbsp;Ω (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202407829-fig-0007">7f</a>). The fact that the equivalent circuit before and after the cycle is the same, indicates that no additional interfacial resistance is generated during the long-term cycling, probably owing to the structure robustness of the 3D carbon-coated interconnected nanoporous structure.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202407829-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202407829-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, we developed a 3D N, S codoped carbon protection strategy on nanoporous MnS for potential industry-scale SIB anode application. The synthesis strategy is simple, scalable, and very economical. The synthesized NS-C@MnS-900 exhibits a record-high reversible capacity of 845&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, excellent high-rate performance, and cycling stability, which is better than all reported MnS-based SIB anodes. These excellent electrochemical properties are attributed to the nanoporous structure design and the N/S doped 3D carbon protection layer, which not only provides a large number of active sites, but also enhances the binding between MnS nano-ligaments and carbon layers, resulting in enhanced Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics and nanostructure stability. These merits make the developed MnS anode very attractive for industrial applications.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202407829-sec-0040">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202407829-sec-0040-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202407829-sec-0050">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202407829-sec-0060">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202407829-sec-0070">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202407829-sec-0070-title"> Materials Preparation</h4>
                  
                  <p>The MnCO<sub>3</sub> (99.5&nbsp;wt.%, Xilong Scientific Corp.) powder was calcined in a tubular furnace at 500&nbsp;°C in the air for 4&nbsp;h with a heating rate of 1 °C&nbsp;min<sup>−1</sup> to obtain black nanoporous Mn<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> particles.</p>
                  
                  <p>Mn<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> of 100.0&nbsp;mg powder was immersed in 1.0&nbsp;mL of aniline solution (99.5&nbsp;wt.%, Macklin Chemical Corp.) at room temperature. After 20&nbsp;h immersion, the mixture was transferred into a corundum boat which was then put at the center of a quartz tube (φ30×φ27×1000&nbsp;mm) furnace. Additionally, another corundum boat with 450&nbsp;mg of 2-aminothiophenol was set next to the first boat. Ar gas (99.99%) was flowed for 10&nbsp;min with 600&nbsp;sccm to create an Ar atmosphere in the quartz tube, and then the gaseous Ar was sealed. Subsequently, the temperature was increased from room temperature to 800/900/1000&nbsp;°C by a speed of 40&nbsp;°C&nbsp;min<sup>−1</sup>. The pyrolysis time was 60&nbsp;min at 800/900/1000&nbsp;°C. After pyrolysis, the furnace was immediately opened, and the quartz tube was cooled with a fan to room temperature. The Mn<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> substrate was sulphurized to MnS during the pyrolysis. The final product NS-C@MnS) was achieved.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202407829-sec-0080">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202407829-sec-0080-title"> Materials Characterization</h4>
                  
                  <p>X-ray diffraction (XRD) test was performed on an X-ray diffractometer with Cu Kα radiation (Rigaku D/max 2500). Scanning electron microscopy (SEM, HITACHI S-4700) and high-resolution transmission electron microscopy (HRTEM, JEOL, JEM-200F) equipped with energy dispersive X-ray spectrometer (EDS) were employed to study the microstructures and elemental mapping distributions. Raman scattering of the sample was identified using a HORIBA LabRAM HR Evolution (France). X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) was recorded with an Al Kα X-ray source (Thermo Scientific K-Alpha). The Brunauer–Emmett–Teller (BET) surface area was evaluated by N<sub>2</sub> adsorption/desorption isotherms using an automated adsorption apparatus (ASAP 2460).</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202407829-sec-0090">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202407829-sec-0090-title"> Na-Ion Battery Test</h4>
                  
                  <p>The electrochemical performances were tested in the CR-2032 coin cell. First, the anode slurry was prepared by uniformly mixing the NS-C@MnS, super P carbon and 3% polyvinylidene fluoride (PVDF) in N-methyl-1,2-pyrrolidone (NMP) solvent at a mass ratio of 6:3:1. Second, the resulting mixture was milled for 12&nbsp;h in a mortar to obtain the final slurry which was then applied to the copper foil current collector to form the electrode. The electrode was dried in a vacuum oven overnight at 120&nbsp;°C, and then it was cut into a disc with a diameter of 12&nbsp;mm. The mass loading of active material was 1.0–1.5&nbsp;mg&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup> for the half-cell test. Finally, the coin cell was assembled in the Ar glove box using a Na chip (diameter = 14&nbsp;mm) as a counter electrode and Celgard 2400 as the separator. The electrolyte was 1 M NaPF<sub>6</sub> in diglyme with a volume ratio of 1:1. The electrochemical performance was conducted on a LAND CT2001A multichannel battery test system at room temperature (25 °C). The test voltage was 0.05–3.00&nbsp;V, and the current rate ranges from 0.1C to 10.0C. CV and electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) tests were conducted on a CHI 660e workstation. CV was tested from 0.05 to 3.00&nbsp;V at 0.1&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>.</p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">

                  <li data-bib-id="smll202407829-bib-0004"><span class="bullet">4</span><span class="author">Y. Y. Zhang</span>, <span class="author">X. X. Yang</span>, <span class="author">Y. X. Hu</span>, <span class="author">K. L. Hu</span>, <span class="author">X. Lin</span>, <span class="author">X. J. Liu</span>, <span class="author">K. M. Reddy</span>, <span class="author">G. Q.                      <div class="extra-links getFTR"><span class="hidden data-doi">10.1002/smll.202200787</span><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div>
                        <span><a href="/servlet/linkout?suffix=null&amp;dbid=32&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202407829&amp;key=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XovVyntbY%253D&amp;getFTLinkType=true&amp;doiForPubOfPage=10.1002%2Fsmll.202407829&amp;refDoi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202200787&amp;linkType=COI&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT&amp;linkLocation=Reference" onclick="newWindow(this.href);return false" class="visitable" target="_blank">CAS</a></span><span><a
